\"string\") {\n    runs.push(new TextRun({ text, size: 22, font: \"Arial\", color: C.text }));\n  } else {\n    text.forEach(t => runs.push(new TextRun({ size: 22, font: \"Arial\", color: C.text, ...t })));\n  }\n  return new Paragraph({\n    numbering: { reference: ref, level: 0 },\n    spacing: { after: 120, line: 300 },\n    children: runs,\n  });\n}\n\nfunction spacer(h = 200) {\n  return new Paragraph({ spacing: { after: h }, children: [] });\n}\n\nfunction accentLine() {\n  return new Paragraph({\n    border: { bottom: { style: BorderStyle.SINGLE, size: 4, color: C.accent, space: 1 }    ],\n          }),\n        ],\n      }),\n    ],\n  });\n}\n\nfunction critiqueBox(titleText, bodyText) {\n  return calloutBox(titleText, bodyText, C.warn, C.warnLight);\n}\n\nfunction responseBox(titleText, bodyText) {\n  return calloutBox(titleText, bodyText, C.green, C.greenLight);\n}\n\n// Numbering configs\nconst numberConfigs = [];\nfor (let i = 0; i < 8; i++) {\n Constraint Engine has no network effects.\n- If the data format is open, any competitor can build their own adaptive engine on the same data. The algorithm itself isn't proprietary if the input/output format is standard.\n- A small startup's adaptive engine will have less training data than a larger competitor entering later. First-mover advantage in ML/AI is weak without exclusive data access.\n\n**Response to Critique 6: \"Timing is now because AI exists\"**\n- AI platforms like Claude, GPT, and Gemini will likely build constraint and guardrail systems natively rather than relying on external tools.
